## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: The target variable dA_dt is the instantaneous rate of change of concentration A in a chemical reaction. In typical kinetics, the rate law expresses dA_dt as a function of the reactant concentration A, possibly with explicit time dependence arising from factors such as catalyst deactivation, temperature changes, or external perturbations. The task belongs clearly to chemical reaction kinetics, where differential rate equations describe reaction mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Power-law kinetics (general order): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (nŌĆæthŌĆæorder reaction where c1 is the reaction order; negative c0 for consumption)
- Parallel firstŌĆæorder and secondŌĆæorder: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (two competing pathways with different molecularities)
- Reversible firstŌĆæorder (net rate): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (forward and backward reactions, e.g., A Ōćī product, with constant reverse source)
- Autocatalytic growth/decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalytic production with limited resource, logistic-type differential form)
- Exponential timeŌĆædecay of rate constant: dA_dt = c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (catalyst deactivation or nonŌĆæisothermal decay)
- PowerŌĆælaw timeŌĆædependence of rate constant: dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * A (timeŌĆævarying rate constant due to e.g., ramping conditions)
- Combined timeŌĆæconcentration scaling: dA_dt = c0 * t**c1 * A**c2 (empirical rate law for nonŌĆæelementary reactions with external influence)
- Substrate inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2) (rate with substrate inhibition, highŌĆæorder denominator)
- HalfŌĆæorder radicalŌĆæchain kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (common in radical polymerization or chain reactions)
- LangmuirŌĆæHinshelwood bimolecular surface reaction: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A)**2 (dualŌĆæsite surface reaction with competitive adsorption)
- Enzymatic reaction with timeŌĆædependent inactivation: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) * exp(-c2 * t) (MichaelisŌĆæMenten rate multiplied by an inactivation exponential)
- Rate with product inhibition (feedback): dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(-c1 * A) (selfŌĆæinhibition approximated by exponential damping)
- Consecutive reaction pseudoŌĆæsteadyŌĆæstate: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (c1 / (A + c2)) (intermediate steadyŌĆæstate approximation yielding rational form)
- Reversible squaredŌĆæterm kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 - c1 * A (forward secondŌĆæorder, reverse firstŌĆæorder)
- Empirical logisticŌĆælike with time shift: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) * exp(-c2 * t) (autocatalytic reaction with decaying catalyst or resource)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Reaction order dominance ŌåÆ powerŌĆælaw scaling dA_dt ŌłØ A^n, with n often integer or halfŌĆæinteger
- Autocatalytic mechanism ŌåÆ rate proportional to A*(cŌĆæA), yielding sigmoidal concentration profile
- TimeŌĆædependent rate constant ŌåÆ dA_dt contains a separate multiplicative function of t, e.g., exp(ŌĆæc*t) or t^c, indicating external decay or drift
- Reversible or offset ŌåÆ presence of an additive constant term in dA_dt signifies a reverse reaction or constant source
- Substrate/product inhibition ŌåÆ rate denominator contains higher powers of A (1 + c1*A + c2*A^2) reflecting binding saturation or inhibition
- Parallel pathways ŌåÆ sum of two or more distinct rate terms (e.g., c0*A + c1*A^2) indicating competing mechanisms
- Radical/chain reactions ŌåÆ fractional reaction order such as 0.5, giving dA_dt ŌłØ sqrt(A)
- Surface catalytic kinetics ŌåÆ rate expressions with denominator (1 + K*A)^n representing LangmuirŌĆæHinshelwood adsorption models
- Enzyme inactivation ŌåÆ product of a MichaelisŌĆæMentenŌĆætype saturation term and a decaying exponential or powerŌĆælaw in time
- SelfŌĆæinhibition/negative feedback ŌåÆ exponential damping of rate with increasing concentration, e.g., exp(ŌĆæc*A), reflecting inhibitory effects

### Candidate 5: Complex rational + sin terms divided by (A+c1)

The sin terms are `A*c4*sin(...)/(A+c1) + c8*sin(...)/(A+c1)`. For this to equal `c*sin(log(A+1))`, we need `(A*c4+c8)/(A+c1)*sin(...)` = constant*sin(...). This requires `(A*c4+c8)/(A+c1)` to be constant, which means c4/1 = c8/c1, i.e., c8=c4*c1. Then the constant is c4. The rational part works as in Candidate 4.

Set c4 = 0.1641, c8 = c4*c1, c6=1, c7=1, c5=0 (phase), c9=0. Wait, let me re-read: `c4*sin(c5 + c6*log(A*c7+1))/(A+c1) * A + c8*sin(c6*log(A*c7+1) + c9)/(A+c1)`.

The two sin terms have different arguments: `sin(c5 + c6*log(A*c7+1))` vs `sin(c6*log(A*c7+1) + c9)`. Set c5=c9, then they're the same. Then `(A*c4 + c8)*sin(c5+c6*log(A*c7+1))/(A+c1)`. Set c8=c4*c1 to make it constant c4. Set c6=1, c7=1, c5=0. This works.

**Candidate 5 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 6: Rational terms only, no sin or log of sin type.

`A┬│c0/(A+c1) + A┬▓c2/(A+c1) + Ac3/(A+c1) + Ac4/(Ac5+c6) + c7/(Ac5+c6)`

The last two terms: `(Ac4+c7)/(Ac5+c6)`. This is a rational function. The GT has sin(log(A+1)) which cannot be represented by rational functions.

**Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 7: `A┬│c0 + Ac1 + c2*log(Ac3+1) + c4*sin(c5*log(Ac6+1)+c7)`

Can't get A┬▓ from remaining terms. No way to produce A┬▓ from sin(log(...)).

### Candidate 18: `Ac0/(A+c1) + A^c2*c3 + c4*sin(c5*log(Ac6+1)+c7)`
